## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring forces), velocity v (damping/self-excitation), and possibly time t (external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator models include Duffing, van der Pol, and driven-damped variants.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling)
- Driven van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven self-excited)
- Softening/hardening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium; even powers (x²) break symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection (negative damping/self-excitation)
- Van der Pol-type terms (1 - x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping: damping at large amplitudes, excitation at small amplitudes
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Cubic position terms (x³) in restoring force indicate Duffing-type hardening (positive coefficient) or softening (negative coefficient) spring behavior
- Products x*v suggest position-dependent damping or energy transfer between kinetic and potential modes
- Absence of explicit time dependence t suggests an autonomous system where phase-space (x,v) description is sufficient
- If acceleration depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative with a potential energy function derivable by integration
- Rational forms like x/(1 + c*x²) can model bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements

Expanding: `0.194830767863936*v*x**2 - 0.194830767863936*v - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-|x|) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

The GT has these components:
1. A term proportional to `v*x**2`
2. A term proportional to `v`
3. A term `x*exp(-|x|)` — this is a non-standard function
4. A term `sin(v)`

The key challenge is the `x*exp(-|x|)` term. None of the candidates contain `exp` terms involving `x`, and none contain `|x|`. Let me check if any candidate could approximate or exactly represent `x*exp(-|x|)`.

The function `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented as a polynomial in x, a power law `x**c`, or `log(cx+1)`, or `sin(cx+d)` for all x values. It's a specific transcendental function.

Similarly, `sin(v)` cannot be exactly represented by polynomials in v (like `v + v**3 + v**5`), `log(cv+1)`, or `v**c` for all v.

Let me check candidates with both flexible x-terms AND sin(v) or flexible v-terms:

**Candidate 42:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*x + c4) + c5*log(c6*v + 1) + c7*x**c8 + c9*v*x**2`
- Has `sin` but in x, not v. Has `log` in v, not sin(v). Cannot match.

**Candidate 36:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*x + c4) + c5*x**c6 + c7*v*x**2 + c8*t*v**5`
- Has sin in x, not v, and has t-dependence. Cannot match.

No candidate has `sin(v)` as a term. So I need to check: can `sin(v)` be represented by the v-terms available? The candidates offer terms like `v`, `v**3`, `v**5`, `v**c`, `log(cv+1)`. None of these can exactly equal `sin(v)` for all v.

Similarly, `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by `x**c` terms, `x**4`, `log(cx+1)`, polynomials in x, etc. for all x.

Since the GT contains both `sin(v)` (which requires a sinusoidal function of v) and `x*exp(-|x|)` (which requires an exponential function of x), and no candidate has both (or either) of these functional forms, no candidate can match.

Wait - let me reconsider. Could `x*exp(-|x|)` be built from combinations of `x**c` terms? No, because `x*exp(-|x|)` decays exponentially for large |x|, while any finite sum of power laws either grows or decays polynomially. These are fundamentally different asymptotic behaviors.

Could `sin(v)` be exactly represented? No candidate has `sin(v)`. The only sin terms are in x (candidates 36, 42). No exact representation of sin(v) exists using polynomials, power laws, or logarithms.

Therefore, no candidate can match the GT.

Expanding: `0.194830767863936*v*x**2 - 0.194830767863936*v - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v*x**2` (coefficient ≈ 0.1948)
2. `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.1948)
3. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` (coefficient ≈ -3.0492)
4. `sin(v)` (coefficient ≈ -0.1430)

Key observations:
- `x*exp(-|x|)` is NOT a polynomial in x. It cannot be represented by any finite combination of power-law terms `x**n`.
- `sin(v)` is NOT a polynomial in v. It cannot be represented by any finite sum of `v**n` terms.

These two transcendental functions are essential and cannot be replicated by polynomials or power laws.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of both `x*exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)`:

**Most candidates** use polynomial-like terms in x (like `x**c3`, `x**4`, `x**3`) and polynomial terms in v (like `v**3`, `v**5`). None of these can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` or `sin(v)`.

- `x**c3` for any fixed c3 is a power law, not `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- `v**3` or `v**5` cannot reproduce `sin(v)`.
- `log(c*x+1)` or `log(c*v+1)` cannot reproduce these either.

**Candidates with sin():** Candidates 36 and 42 have `sin(c3*x + c4)`, which is sin of x, not sin of v. This cannot match `sin(v)`.

**Candidates with exp():** Candidates 17, 23, 24, 26 have `exp(c*t)`, which depends on t, not on x. Even setting the coefficient to 0 eliminates the term entirely, and we still need `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**No candidate** contains both:
- A term like `x*exp(-|x|)` or any exponential function of x
- A term like `sin(v)`

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)` are linearly independent from all polynomial/power-law basis functions, no candidate can match the GT.
